"And they've never forgotten that."</p><p class="">This is mostly false. It was Hillary Clinton, then the first lady, who used the word "superpredator" to advocate for the 1994 crime bill that Biden co-wrote more than 30 years ago. Biden <a href="https://www.cnn.com/2019/03/07/politics/biden-1993-speech-predators/index.html" target="_blank">did warn of "predators"</a> in a floor speech in support of his bill, however.</p><div Timm  and Adam Edelman</p><div class="timestamps founders-mono f2" data-test="timestamp">18d ago / 6:13 AM UTC</div></div></div><h2 data-test="headline" class="cardTitle___2kTZx">Fact-check: Biden says Trump &#x27;paid a total of $750 in taxes&#x27;</h2><p class="">Biden, during a prolonged exchange over the amount of federal taxes Trump has paid, said, "This guy paid a total of $750 in taxes."</p><p class="">Trump retorted by saying, "I've paid millions of dollars in taxes, millions of dollars of income tax."</p><p class="">Biden's claim accurately reflects new reporting by The New York Times for 2016 and 2017.</p><p class="">Trump's federal income tax <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2020/09/29/us/trump-750-taxes.html?referringSource=articleShare">bill was just $750 the year</a> he won the presidency,<a href="https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2020/09/27/us/donald-trump-taxes.html"> The Times reported after obtaining and reviewing more than two decades of the president's tax information</a>. During his first year in office, his bill remained $750. The information doesn't include his returns from 2018 and 2019.</p><p class="">According to The Times, Trump had paid no income taxes at all in 10 of the 15 years before 2016, because he reported losing much more money than he made during that time. NBC News hasn't seen or verified any of the documents reported by The Times.Â </p><div class="df justify-start mt6 lh-none socialShareList socialWrapper___IoCOr dn-print" data-test="timestamp">18d ago / 6:18 AM UTC</div></div></div><h2 data-test="headline" class="cardTitle___2kTZx">Fact-check: Does Trump support cutting police funding?</h2><p class="">"His budget calls for a $400 million cut in local law enforcement assistance," Biden said, reiterating his own opposition to defunding the police.Â </p><p class="">That is mostly true, although Biden actually undercounts the proposed cuts. While Trump has opposed calls from some Democrats to reduce police funding in response to the deaths of George Floyd and other Black Americans over the summer, the Trump administration's budget proposal does, indeed, call for big cuts for several police programs.</p><p class="">In the Justice Department's <a href="https://www.justice.gov/doj/page/file/1246736/download#page=13">budget plan</a> for fiscal year 2021, the Trump administration requested $1.51 billion for over 50 programs funding state and local law enforcement.Â That number would cut about $515 million from previous fiscal years, in part by slashing budgets for a number of Obama-era programs, including initiatives that provided body cameras for police officers.</p><div class="df justify-start mt6 lh-none data-test="timestamp">18d ago / 6:22 AM UTC</div></div></div><h2 data-test="headline" class="cardTitle___2kTZx">Fact-check: Trump says he took advantage of a tax code Biden could have fixed</h2><p class="">During an acrimonious exchange, the president defended the low tax bill he is reported to have paid by suggesting that if Biden wanted him to have not taken advantage of the tax code, he should have acted to fix it during his tenure in the Senate.</p><p class="">"The tax code that put him in a position that he pays less tax than a schoolteacher is because of â he says he's smart because he can take advantage of the tax code. And he does take advantage of the tax code," Biden said.</p><p class="">Trump replied: "But why didn't you do it over the last 25 years? Why didn't you do it over the last 25 years?"</p><p class="">In reality, despite being in Senate for 36 years, Biden was never technically in a position to rewrite the federal tax code.</p><p class="">While in the Senate from 1973 to 2009, Biden was chair of the Judiciary and Foreign Relations committees and had no direct hand in writing tax laws. That's the job of the Finance Committee.</p><p class="">Trump, on the other hand, takes advantage of several loopholes to avoid paying taxes, including some for which he personally lobbied.Â </p><p class="">Among them is a law passed in 1986 to limit investors not actively involved in a business from taking deductions and attributing losses against their incomes. An "at risk" rule was also added to prevent taxpayers from deducting losses greater than their investments. But Congress largely exempted real estate developers, like Trump.</p><p class="">At the same time that his investments in Atlantic City, New Jersey, were suffering, <a href="https://youtu.be/AXO2936XM9w?t=683">Trump appeared before Congress in 1991 to advocate for "tax shelters"</a> that would "incentivize" "investment in real estate" to help boost the economy during the recession.</p><div class="df justify-start mt6 lh-none socialShareList socialWrapper___IoCOr dn-print" data-test="social-share-list"><input type="checkbox" class="dn" 90-minute debate quickly descended into chaos after Trump began to interrupt both Biden and the moderator, Fox News' Chris Wallace. The night didn't get much calmer from there.</p><div class="ad tc tl-m ad-container boxinlineAd dn-print" data-test="ad__container"><div data-enigma="true" data-slot="boxinline" article-body__content w-100 mh0 mb8 fn overflow-x-hidden card___2nUEE" id="ncrd1241486" data-sort-time="2020-09-30T02:24:00.000Z" data-update-time="2020-09-30T06:14:51.000Z" data-test="thumbnail"><div class="lazyload-wrapper"><div style="height:50px" class="lazyload-placeholder"></div></div></div><div class="df flex-column"><p class="f4 founders-cond mv0 gray-80" data-test="byline">Jane C. Timm </p><div class="timestamps founders-mono f2" data-test="timestamp">18d ago / 6:14 AM UTC</div></div></div><h1 data-test="headline" class="cardTitle___2kTZx">Fact-check: Did Biden call Black Americans &#x27;superpredators&#x27;?</h1><p class="">"Look at the crime bill, 1994, where you called them 'superpredators,' African Americans are 'superpredators,'" Trump said. "And they've never forgotten that."</p><p class="">This is mostly false. It was Hillary Clinton, then the first lady, who used the word "superpredator" to advocate for the 1994 crime bill that Biden co-wrote more than 30 years ago. Biden <a href="https://www.cnn.com/2019/03/07/politics/biden-1993-speech-predators/index.html" target="_blank">did warn of "predators"</a> in a floor speech in support of his bill, however.</p><div class="df justify-start mt6 lh-none socialShareList socialWrapper___IoCOr dn-print" data-test="social-share-list"><input type="checkbox" class="dn" data-test="social-menu__checkbox" class="socialListIcon___9xobL"><a Timm  and Adam Edelman</p><div class="timestamps founders-mono f2" data-test="timestamp">18d ago / 6:13 AM UTC</div></div></div><h2 data-test="headline" class="cardTitle___2kTZx">Fact-check: Biden says Trump &#x27;paid a total of $750 in taxes&#x27;</h2><p class="">Biden, during a prolonged exchange over the amount of federal taxes Trump has paid, said, "This guy paid a total of $750 in taxes."</p><p class="">Trump retorted by saying, "I've paid millions of dollars in taxes, millions of dollars of income tax."</p><p class="">Biden's claim accurately reflects new reporting by The New York Times for 2016 and 2017.</p><p class="">Trump's federal income tax <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2020/09/29/us/trump-750-taxes.html?referringSource=articleShare">bill was just $750 the year</a> he won the presidency,<a href="https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2020/09/27/us/donald-trump-taxes.html"> The Times reported after obtaining and reviewing more than two decades of the president's tax information</a>. During his first year in office, his bill remained $750. The information doesn't include his returns from 2018 and 2019.</p><p class="">According to The Times, Trump had paid no income taxes at all in 10 of the 15 years before 2016, because he reported losing much more money than he made during that time. NBC News hasn't seen or verified any of the documents reported by The Times.Â </p><div class="df justify-start mt6 lh-none socialShareList socialWrapper___IoCOr dn-print" for a $400 million cut in local law enforcement assistance," Biden said, reiterating his own opposition to defunding the police.Â </p><p class="">That is mostly true, although Biden actually undercounts the proposed cuts. While Trump has opposed calls from some Democrats to reduce police funding in response to the deaths of George Floyd and other Black Americans over the summer, the Trump administration's budget proposal does, indeed, call for big cuts for several police programs.</p><p class="">In the Justice Department's <a href="https://www.justice.gov/doj/page/file/1246736/download#page=13">budget plan</a> for fiscal year 2021, the Trump administration requested $1.51 billion for over 50 programs funding state and local law enforcement.Â That number would cut about $515 million from previous fiscal years, in part by slashing budgets for a number of Obama-era programs, including initiatives that provided body cameras for police officers.</p><div class="df justify-start mt6 lh-none data-test="timestamp">18d ago / 6:22 AM UTC</div></div></div><h2 data-test="headline" class="cardTitle___2kTZx">Fact-check: Trump says he took advantage of a tax code Biden could have fixed</h2><p class="">During an acrimonious exchange, the president defended the low tax bill he is reported to have paid by suggesting that if Biden wanted him to have not taken advantage of the tax code, he should have acted to fix it during his tenure in the Senate.</p><p class="">"The tax code that put him in a position that he pays less tax than a schoolteacher is because of â he says he's smart because he can take advantage of the tax code. And he does take advantage of the tax code," Biden said.</p><p class="">Trump replied: "But why didn't you do it over the last 25 years? Why didn't you do it over the last 25 years?"</p><p class="">In reality, despite being in Senate for 36 years, Biden was never technically in a position to rewrite the federal tax code.</p><p class="">While in the Senate from 1973 to 2009, Biden was chair of the Judiciary and Foreign Relations committees and had no direct hand in writing tax laws. That's the job of the Finance Committee.</p><p class="">Trump, on the other hand, takes advantage of several loopholes to avoid paying taxes, including some for which he personally lobbied.Â </p><p class="">Among them is a law passed in 1986 to limit investors not actively involved in a business from taking deductions and attributing losses against their incomes. An "at risk" rule was also added to prevent taxpayers from deducting losses greater than their investments. But Congress largely exempted real estate developers, like Trump.</p><p class="">At the same time that his investments in Atlantic City, New Jersey, were suffering, <a href="https://youtu.be/AXO2936XM9w?t=683">Trump appeared before Congress in 1991 to advocate for "tax shelters"</a> that would "incentivize" "investment in real estate" to help boost the economy during the recession.</p><div class="df justify-start mt6 lh-none socialShareList socialWrapper___IoCOr dn-print" data-test="social-share-list"><input type="checkbox" class="dn"
